Bioinformatics. 2009;25:20789. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/btp352&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR124" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2666">124</a>]. Read counting per gene was performed using the count command of HTSeq [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 130" title="Anders S, Pyl PT, Huber W. HTSeq--a Python framework to work with high-throughput sequencing data. Bioinformatics. 2015;31:1669. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/btu638&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR130" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2669">130</a>] and reads per kilobase mapped (rpkm) expression values were calculated with edgeR [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 131" title="Robinson MD, McCarthy DJ, Smyth GK. edgeR: a Bioconductor package for differential expression analysis of digital gene expression data. Bioinformatics. 2010;26:13940. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/btp616&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR131" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2672">131</a>]. Only genes with an rpkm 1 in at least one sample were considered in further analyses.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Annotation lift-over to 10 Genomics diploid assemblies</h3><p>Our reference genome annotation was transferred independently for each of the inferred haplotypes derived from our 10 Genomics de novo assemblies of female and male genomes using UCSC Genome Browsers utilities [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 132" title="Kent WJ, Baertsch R, Hinrichs A, Miller W, Haussler D. Evolutions cauldron: duplication, deletion, and rearrangement in the mouse and human genomes. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 2003;100:114849. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1073/pnas.1932072100&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR132" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2683">132</a>]. First, a pairwise alignment between each haplotype and the non-redundant reference genome was generated as described above with LAST v926 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 119" title="Kiebasa SM, Wan R, Sato K, Horton P, Frith MC. Adaptive seeds tame genomic sequence comparison. Genome Res. 2011;21:48793. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1101/gr.113985.110&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR119" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2686">119</a>]. Alignments were then converted into a series of syntenic chains and nets, tuned for more divergent genomes (axtChain -linearGap=loose), using the same scoring matrix generated during the LAST alignments. Finally, annotations were moved to the haplotype assemblies using the liftOver utility with a minimum 75% ratio of mapped bases between features. Only the longest isoform of each gene was considered in the lift-over. With this approach, we transferred ~25,159 genes per diploid haplotype or ~80% of the complete annotation.</p><p>We further attempted to recover additional genes not lifted initially by aligning each gene individually back to the haplotype assemblies with BLAT v170523 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 133" title="Kent WJ. BLAT--the BLAST-like alignment tool. Genome Res. 2002;12:65664. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1101/gr.229202&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR133" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2692">133</a>], (-minIdentity=30 -minScore=12 -stepSize=5 -repMatch=2253 -extendThroughN), keeping the highest-scoring alignment for each query. In order to avoid potential problems caused by the BLAT alignment of paralogous sequences, we counted the average number of haplotypes aligned to each reference gene (for a fully phased diploid region we expect 2 haplotypes). These counts were then bootstrapped with 1000 iterations, and all alignments for which the haplotype coverage was below the lower bootstrap 95% confidence interval (~1.6 coverage) were excluded. This procedure recovered an average of 364 additional genes per haplotype.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Divergence analysis of diploid genotypes</h3><p>We calculated rates of divergence at synonymous (<i>d</i><sub>S</sub>) and non-synonymous (<i>d</i><sub>N</sub>) sites between the coding sequences of diploid genotypes for each sex separately. In order to further increase the number of genes analyzed in the SDR, we additionally made use of the resolved haplotypes derived from the female PacBio assembly (from scaffolds 163 and 225). We identified orthologous genes with BLASTP using an <i>e</i> value threshold of 110<sup>3</sup> and only considering the top hit for each gene. This process recovered an additional set of 11 genes that have not been previously lifted-up to the 10 Genomics diploid assembly. Only sequences with a valid start codon, without internal stop codons and with a minimum sequence length of 120 bases, were analyzed. After this initial filter, pairwise alignments for the two haplotypes were obtained with PRANK v140603 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 134" title="Lytynoja A, Goldman N. An algorithm for progressive multiple alignment of sequences with insertions. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 2005;102:1055762. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1073/pnas.0409137102&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR134" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2717">134</a>], and <i>d</i><sub>S</sub> and <i>d</i><sub>N</sub> estimates were calculated using the method of Yang and Nielsen [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 135" title="Yang Z, Nielsen R. Estimating synonymous and nonsynonymous substitution rates under realistic evolutionary models. Mol Biol Evol. 2000;17:3243. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/oxfordjournals.molbev.a026236&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR135" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2728">135</a>] as implemented in the yn00 program of PAML v4.9h [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 136" title="Yang Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol Biol Evol. 2007;24:158691. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/molbev/msm088&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR136" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2731">136</a>]. Pairwise comparisons with <i>d</i><sub>S</sub>&gt;0.2 were excluded, thereby avoiding the incorrect assignment of orthologs.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Phylogenetic analysis</h3><p>We used gene trees to determine the relative age of recombination suppression for the haplotypes in each identified sex chromosome strata. In addition to our non-redundant <i>S. viminalis</i> genome, coding sequences for <i>S. suchowensis</i> v4.1 and <i>P. trichocarpa</i> v10.1 were obtained from PopGenie v3 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Sjdin A, Street NR, Sandberg G, Gustafsson P, Jansson S. The Populus Genome Integrative Explorer (PopGenIE): a new resource for exploring the Populus genome. New Phytologist. 2009;182:101325. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1111/j.1469-8137.2009.02807.x&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2756">62</a>] and sequences for <i>S. purpurea</i> v1.0 were obtained from Phytozome v12 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 137" title="Goodstein DM, Shu S, Howson R, et al. Phytozome: a comparative platform for green plant genomics. Nucleic Acids Res. 2012;40:D117886. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/nar/gkr944&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR137" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2763">137</a>]. Only the longest transcripts were considered. We first use the conditional reciprocal best BLAST method [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 138" title="Aubry S, Kelly S, Kmpers BM, Smith-Unna RD, Hibberd JM. Deep evolutionary comparison of gene expression identifies parallel recruitment of trans-factors in two independent origins of C4 photosynthesis. PLoS Genet. 2014;10:e1004365. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pgen.1004365&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR138" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2766">138</a>], with a BLAST <i>e</i> value cutoff &lt;110<sup>5</sup>, to identify 14,255 one-to-one orthologs across all four species (<i>S. viminalis</i>, <i>S. suchawensis</i>, <i>S. purpurea</i>, and <i>P. trichocarpa</i>). For each ortholog group, we searched for the <i>S. viminalis</i> homolog in the lifted annotation of the female and male phased diploid assemblies and aligned all species sequences with MAFFT v7.313 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 139" title="Katoh K, Standley DM. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol Biol Evol. 2013;30:77280. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/molbev/mst010&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR139" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2790">139</a>]. Aligned columns with &gt;40% gaps and taxa with &gt;40% of missing data were removed. Maximum likelihood phylogenetic trees were obtained with RAxML v8.2.12 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 140" title="Stamatakis A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics. 2014;30:13123. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/btu033&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR140" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2793">140</a>] using the rapid bootstrap algorithm with 100 bootstraps and the GTRGAMMA model of sequence evolution. Trees were rooted in the <i>P. trichocarpa</i> branch and were only considered if the two female haplotypes were present. Phylogenetic tree analyses were performed with ETE3 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 141" title="Huerta-Cepas J, Serra F, Bork P. ETE 3: reconstruction, analysis, and visualization of phylogenomic data. Mol Biol Evol. 2016;33:16358. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1093/molbev/msw046&#xA;&#xA;." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR141" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2800">141</a>].</p></div></div></section>
                    <section aria-labelledby="availability-of-data-and-materials" data-title="Availability of data and materials"><div class="c-article-section" id="availability-of-data-and-materials-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="availability-of-data-and-materials">Availability of data and materials</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="availability-of-data-and-materials-content">
              
              <p>Genome sequencing data and annotation generated for this study have all been deposited in EBIs ENA (<a href="https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ena">https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ena</a>) under project number PRJEB31619 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 142" title="Almeida P, Proux-Wera E, Churcher A et al. Genome assembly of the basket willow, Salix viminalis, reveals earliest stages of sex chromosome expansion. Supplementary Datasets. 2020. ENA accesion: PRJEB31619." href="/articles/10.1186/s12915-020-00808-1#ref-CR142" id="ref-link-section-d6089e2870">142</a>]. The datasets used and/or analyzed during the current study are available from the corresponding author on reasonable request.</p>

JEM also gratefully acknowledges further the support from a Royal Society Wolfson Merit Award, a Canada 150 Research Chair, and the Natural Sciences and Engineering Research Council of Canada. Sequencing and annotation were funded by the Swedish Energy Agency, grant 30599-5, and from the Swedish Research Council for Environment, Agricultural Sciences and Spatial Planning (Formas) grant 2016-20031. Sequencing was performed by the National Genomics Infrastructure (NGI) Sweden at Science for Life Laboratory. EP-W, AC, LS, JD, JN, and BN were financially supported by the Swedish Research Council and the Knut and Alice Wallenberg Foundation as part of NGI and NBIS (National Bioinformatics Infrastructure Sweden) at SciLifeLab.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="author-information" data-title="Author information"><div class="c-article-section" id="author-information-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="author-information">Author information</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="author-information-content"><span class="c-article-author-information__subtitle u-visually-hidden" id="author-notes">Author notes</span><ol class="c-article-author-information__list"><li class="c-article-author-information__item" id="na1"><p>Sofia Berlin and Judith E.                 <div class="c-article-supplementary__item" data-test="supp-item" id="MOESM1"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="https://static-content.springer.com/esm/art%3A10.1186%2Fs12915-020-00808-1/MediaObjects/12915_2020_808_MOESM1_ESM.pdf" data-supp-info-image=""><b>Additional file 1: Table S1.</b></a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p> Whole-genome DNA sequencing data used in this study. <b>Table S2.</b> Assembly statistics for the full and non-redundant assemblies of <i>Salix viminalis</i>. <b>Table S3.</b> Characterization of the different annotation classes for the <i>Salix viminalis</i> assembly. <b>Table S4.</b> Characterization of heterozygous structural variations identified in Chr15. <b>Table S5.</b> List of all genes found on putatively W-linked scaffolds. <b>Figure S1.</b> Whole genome synteny between <i>Salix viminalis</i> assembly and <i>Populus trichocarpa</i>. <b>Figure S2</b>.
